        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer122807855" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15236667455322168037">Late Eclipses was a magnificent read. Exactly as I've come to expect of Seanan McGuire. <br/><br/><br/><br/>Aside from the excellent world building, blending of traditional lore with the modern world, characterisations and storylines (both for Late Eclipses alone and across the series); it's sheer joy to read such good word craft written in an active voice. <br/><br/><br/><br/>Late Eclipses was a tantalisingly dark read but with enough interest in and care for the characters developed that it really mattered to me what becames of them</span>
  <span id="freeText15236667455322168037" style="display:none">Late Eclipses was a magnificent read. Exactly as I've come to expect of Seanan McGuire. <br /><br /><br /><br />Aside from the excellent world building, blending of traditional lore with the modern world, characterisations and storylines (both for Late Eclipses alone and across the series); it's sheer joy to read such good word craft written in an active voice. <br /><br /><br /><br />Late Eclipses was a tantalisingly dark read but with enough interest in and care for the characters developed that it really mattered to me what becames of them and how. You feel for their losses and share their little joys and feel Toby's exhaustion as you read. <br /><br /><br /><br />There are important revelations pertinent to the series arc and future books but Late Eclipses is complete in and of itself, so there's no distaste of cliffhanger to deal with, just the tingly anticipation of the release of One Salt Sea to come. <br /><br /><br /><br />I'm glad that Seanan McGuire is such a prolific writer of such excellent quality. It's a rare gift and we're lucky to receive the benefits of her output. <br /><br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8339561124409416460">4.5<br/><br/>Yes, it has flaws. Yes, Toby is frustrating when she keeps running back into danger. Yes, it’s ridiculously entertaining, addictive & wonderful. </span>
  <span id="freeText8339561124409416460" style="display:none">4.5<br /><br />Yes, it has flaws. Yes, Toby is frustrating when she keeps running back into danger. Yes, it’s ridiculously entertaining, addictive &amp; wonderful. </span>

      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review3019351802">
  <td colspan="2">

<div id="review_123454574" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/123454574" />
    <a title="Torzilla" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3322973-torzilla"><img alt="Torzilla" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1301449340p2/3322973.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/123454574?book_show_action=true">Sep 25, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Torzilla" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Torzilla" href="/user/show/3322973-torzilla">Torzilla</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3322973-torzilla?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3322973-torzilla?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer123454574" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8814944399167410457">LATE ECLIPSES, book four in the <i>October Daye</i> series, delivers a tightly woven plot which manages to skewer our perception of what Toby is in the process. If one is interested in learning more about Toby's world, this novel is the novel to read. If, however, the reader is searching for more of a romance, he or she will be severely disappointed with this installment.<br/><br/>I always felt the world-building was Seanan's strong point when it came to the Fae world. She has something refreshing to incorporate</span>
  <span id="freeText8814944399167410457" style="display:none">LATE ECLIPSES, book four in the <i>October Daye</i> series, delivers a tightly woven plot which manages to skewer our perception of what Toby is in the process. If one is interested in learning more about Toby's world, this novel is the novel to read. If, however, the reader is searching for more of a romance, he or she will be severely disappointed with this installment.<br /><br />I always felt the world-building was Seanan's strong point when it came to the Fae world. She has something refreshing to incorporate into each additional book, and like I said before, LATE ECLIPSES tops all its predecessors. Not only are new races and characters introduced, but we also learn more about some of the current characters and their lifestyles. <br /><br />Unlike past books, LATE ECLIPSES has the perfect balance of action and investigating, and thus, was a book I was unable to put down. A word of warning: it might take a few chapters to finally get invested within this story, but once Toby reaches the Queen's court, the story picked up and continued on strong.<br /><br />I still don't entirely understand May's purpose in this series, but that doesn't bother me as much this time around because the plot line follows Toby and Amandine's past. I had a few questions from past books answered, and now I have a whole new set to ponder over as I wait for the fifth book in this series.<br /><br />The beginning was actually one of my two complaints. For some reason, and this might be because I'm weird, I felt the characters were off. Tybalt wasn't the cranky King of Cats I grew to love, May annoyed me because of how chipper she was, and Toby seemed off because she was so... normal. I'm not entirely sure what that says about me if I get freaked out about the heroine acting normal and happy. Either way, I'd love to hear if others agree or disagree with my feelings on the start.<br /><br />The romance--or lack thereof--was my second complaint. I appreciated every moment Toby and Tybalt shared, and wished there were more for me to squeal over. Instead, when Tybalt stepped aside, I was left feeling frustrated because of Connor's presence.<br /><br />While Tybalt is typically in control, Connor is like the needy, clingy boy (which is the reason why I do not like him as a love interest for Toby--she needs someone in control and who can keep her levelheaded, like in that one scene...). Every time he went to hold Toby's hand, I wanted to shake Toby and remind her of Tybalt, and then at one point, I literally groaned out loud because of what happened. I won't say what, but I am not happy about those chain of events and how that may affect later books in the series. <br /><br />I wish, instead of focusing on making Tybalt and Connor rivals for Toby's attention/affections--which seems to be what Toby <i>would</i> comment and focus on--we could see more focus on Toby and Tybalt's relationship. At the very least, I wish we were granted more of a reaction on Toby's part. She would register what what would happen, but that was the extent of her thoughts on the matter.<br /><br />Perhaps this is another instance of me being weird, because the whole idea of the married seal hitting on our heroine freaks me out. Besides, why do I want to read about Connor and Toby getting all cuddly when we've got the sexy King of Cats vying for Toby's affections? Again, that's my personal opinion, and I'm sure there are some readers out there who will feel the complete opposite.<br /><br />LATE ECLIPSES wasn't my favorite book out of the series character-wise, but I did enjoy it more so than earlier books when it came to learning about Toby's past and the plot. Despite my complaints about the romance aspect--which really was a minor one when it comes to this story, because the plot line is so engaging--I still suggest readers pick up the latest installment to the October Daye series as soon as they possibly can. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8814944399167410457" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_965312307" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/965312307" />
    <a title="Maria Dimitrova" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15922517-maria-dimitrova"><img alt="Maria Dimitrova" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1563534668p2/15922517.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria Dimitrova" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria Dimitrova" href="/user/show/15922517-maria-dimitrova">Maria Dimitrova</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15922517-maria-dimitrova?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15922517-maria-dimitrova?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15922517-maria-dimitrova?shelf=br-bbb-2016">br-bbb-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15922517-maria-dimitrova?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer965312307" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16202339787226636166"><b> Buddy read with the UF maniacs at <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164' rel='nofollow noopener'>BB&B</a></b><br/><br/><br/>And we're back for our weekly exploration of Faerie with the one and only October Christine Daye! This time we almost didn't make it out alive. The series is getting expressively darker and you know what? I love it! Even when the fear for Toby's live (well mostly the fear for the lives of the people around her since the series has a few more books in it so the likelihood of Toby dying in the middle of the series are slim to none) kept me awake. As usually w</span>
  <span id="freeText16202339787226636166" style="display:none"><b> Buddy read with the UF maniacs at <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164" rel="nofollow noopener">BB&amp;B</a></b><br /><br /><br />And we're back for our weekly exploration of Faerie with the one and only October Christine Daye! This time we almost didn't make it out alive. The series is getting expressively darker and you know what? I love it! Even when the fear for Toby's live (well mostly the fear for the lives of the people around her since the series has a few more books in it so the likelihood of Toby dying in the middle of the series are slim to none) kept me awake. As usually with me I'm deep into full blown obsession with this world (it's either that or I don't care for a book) and I just can't get enough. I love how it makes me feel alive (mostly by making me cry my eyes out but still).<br /><br />Toby's in deep sh*t now with pretty much everyone gunning for her and with her friends dying off like flies. The usual suspects have ganged up on her and are doing their best to make her take the fall for her friends deaths. They even try to make her believe she's the one who's killing them. There were some pretty emotional moments <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Lily's death, Luna's almost dying, that scene with the kitten in the Court of Cats, Raj's mother's death, Rayseline's betrayal (mostly because of the way it must be killing Sylvester, cause I couldn't care less for the vicious bitch), almost loosing Spike (I would have called the UF posse over at BB&amp;B to riot if Spike had died!) and so on  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> when I felt like I was suffocating with grief. I know I'm just 4 books in but these characters have become close and dear friends. Toby's one lucky changeling. Not because she's lucky in the traditional sense of the word. Quite the opposite in fact. But because those same friends are her friends. And they would fight for her as hard as she fights for them and they did in this instalment. I loved how they never gave up even when she did. Toby was in so much trouble this time that even her crazy Mom made an appearance! And Amandine is one of the biggest mysteries in the series so far. With all that happened and all that was implied I feel like the next several books will keep the trend of getting darker.<br /><br />But it wasn't gloom and darkness and death all the way. There were light-hearted moments too. Not much but they were there. Mainly thanks to May and Tybalt. I love that cat! He can be so sweet and so smug at the same time. And he really cares about Toby. The only one who seems to be blind to his affection is Toby herself. May was awesome and she's becoming one of my favourites pretty damn fast. My main complaint about this book was that it had too little of the Luidaeg. I missed the cranky old bat. Those few pages at the end of the book were not enough! <br /><br />With all the things that happened in this book I can barely wait for the next one. But I'll have to wait for the other brave souls that explore the dangerous and treacherous Faerie world of Ms. McGuire to join me next week. Same place, same time, Ladies!</span>
  <a data-text-id="16202339787226636166" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_436652619" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/436652619" />
    <a title="VampireNovelFan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4897902-vampirenovelfan"><img alt="VampireNovelFan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1296445543p2/4897902.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/436652619?book_show_action=true">Oct 18, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="VampireNovelFan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="VampireNovelFan" href="/user/show/4897902-vampirenovelfan">VampireNovelFan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4897902-vampirenovelfan?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4897902-vampirenovelfan?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4897902-vampirenovelfan?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4897902-vampirenovelfan?shelf=fae">fae</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer436652619" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer588788624667173161"><a href='http://vampirenovelfan.wordpress.com/2012/10/22/late-eclipses-october-daye-4-its-like-night-and-daye-reading-october-in-october/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <b>It’s like night and…daye! Reading October in October!</b>
</a><br/><br/>This marks my first review of Seanan McGuire's popular series. Normally I prefer to review every book after I read it; however, for this series it was super difficult to become invested early on. I got through the first three quickly to keep my enthusiasm up for the series. But since I read them quickly I didn't think I could write a proper review. But due to the high acclaim that the later books have received I decided to push through, an</span>
  <span id="freeText588788624667173161" style="display:none"><a href="http://vampirenovelfan.wordpress.com/2012/10/22/late-eclipses-october-daye-4-its-like-night-and-daye-reading-october-in-october/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>It’s like night and…daye! Reading October in October!</b>
</a><br /><br />This marks my first review of Seanan McGuire's popular series. Normally I prefer to review every book after I read it; however, for this series it was super difficult to become invested early on. I got through the first three quickly to keep my enthusiasm up for the series. But since I read them quickly I didn't think I could write a proper review. But due to the high acclaim that the later books have received I decided to push through, and that turned out to be a good decision.<br /><br />October "Toby" Daye, our favorite half-human, half-fae, is just a magnet for trouble. She means well, but when it comes to Faerie politics, nothing is cut and dry. She earns knighthood, an unprecedented achievement for a changeling since their kind are all but shunned when it comes to the fae community. So there is definitely an ulterior motive involved...perhaps the perfect scenario to make Toby public enemy number 1 after a number of grave incidents happen to those closest to her. <br /><br />This is far and away the best book of the series so far. it's the most emotionally charged book yet where loyalties are cemented, secrets are revealed, and the action is steady. Everything is a close call, keeping the suspense high. I really didn't know what to expect from page to page for the majority of the book. We find out who Toby's friends really are and just how far they are willing to go to protect her. Her friends aren't perfect, but they're honorable. <br /><br />I finally found myself really starting to like the side characters. My favorite supporting characters are Tybalt, the Luidaeg, Connor, and May. Being the cat person that I am, I do wish Tybalt would get more page time. Though not my favorite, I do like Sylvester and sympathized with him quite a bit. Everyone is coming into their own, and more than willing to prove their worth. The character development is pretty compelling, especially when it comes to Toby and May. The mythology involving the plethora of fairie species evolves quite a bit, expanding the world even more. They are more vulnerable than we think and I'm interested in seeing where things will go next.<br /><br />It's not the first series to have a slow beginning. My favorite series, The Hollows, is the same way (though I became invested faster). I am glad that I stuck through it though because it's definitely one of the best that urban fantasy has to offer. Book 1 to book 4 is literally like night and...daye. <br /><br />*Review also posted to <a href="http://www.amazon.com/review/RSBL3SDPMZ104/ref=cm_cr_pr_perm?ie=UTF8&amp;ASIN=B004I1JC7E&amp;linkCode=&amp;nodeID=&amp;tag=" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="588788624667173161" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('kOFZe1Zy+wnvmh2hTKstkHtV9qs6rpO90+JieXnmH0IpNuFg0C9KaD5M71yJUN3EDzivp1edTL9AeYdr+3vYkA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('8oa0bOty8JmIam+15im/z/s59hU59rqGH1sDYxOQXGlLUQx3bS9B+Fm8nUgj0k+bj1SvGVTFZYSMwOZxkQ2buw==')})
  }

To top everything off, her best friend has been forever changed by her time spent captive in Faerie.\n\nBut the personal takes a backseat to the professional when a mysterious suicide occurs in Nekros City and Alex is hired to investigate. The shade she raises has no memory of the days leading up to his brutal ending, so despite the very public apparent suicide, this is murder. But what kind of magic can overcome the human will to survive? And why does the shade lack the memory of his death?   <span id="freeText7910035215506502237" style="display:none">Hi! I'm Seanan McGuire, author of the Toby Daye series (<i>Rosemary and Rue</i>, <i>A Local Habitation</i>, <i>An Artificial Night</i>, <i>Late Eclipses</i>), as well as a lot of other things. I'm also Mira Grant (<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.miragrant.com">www.miragrant.com</a>), author of <i>Feed</i> and <i>Deadline</i>.<br /><br />Born and raised in Northern California, I fear weather and am remarkably laid-back about rattlesnakes. I watch too many horror movies, read too many comic books, and share my house with two monsters in feline form, Lilly and Alice (Siamese and Maine Coon).<br /><br />I <i>do not</i> check this inbox. Please don't send me messages through Goodreads; they won't be answered. I don't want to have to delete this account. :(</span>
